## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is the acceleration of an oscillator expressed in state variables (x, v) and possibly explicit time dependence t. Nonlinear harmonic oscillators are typically modeled as a restoring force in x plus damping in v and optional external/parametric forcing in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear (damped) harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (small-amplitude oscillations with viscous damping)
- Undamped conservative oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (ideal mass-spring with no dissipation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring with damping)
- Quadratic stiffness nonlinearity: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x * Abs(x) - c2 * v (asymmetric/geometry-induced stiffness; odd restoring force via x|x|)
- Pendulum-like restoring force: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle oscillations with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillator with nonlinear damping and limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity feedback producing self-oscillation)
- Dry (Coulomb) friction model: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * (v / (Abs(v) + c3)) (stick-slip-like dissipation approximated smoothly)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-type damping proportional to v|v|)
- Driven oscillator (external forcing): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodically forced response and resonance)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear resonance, bistability, jump phenomena)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness leading to parametric resonance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring forces typically depend only on x and are odd in x (e.g., -c*x, -c*x**3, -c*sin(c*x)); this encodes symmetry about x=0 for many oscillators.
- Damping terms typically depend on v and are odd in v (e.g., -c*v, -c*v*Abs(v), -c*v**3); oddness enforces energy dissipation independent of velocity sign.
- Self-excited oscillations/limit cycles often appear as state-dependent damping like (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v, which injects energy at small amplitude and dissipates at large amplitude.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness is commonly indicated by the sign and presence of an x**3 term in the restoring force, producing amplitude-dependent frequency and possible bistability under forcing.
- Periodic external forcing is naturally represented by +c*cos(c*t) or +c*sin(c*t) added to dv_dt, producing resonance/beat phenomena when the forcing frequency matches the natural frequency.
- Parametric resonance is indicated by time-varying stiffness multiplying x, e.g., -(c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x, rather than an additive forcing term.
- Non-smooth friction effects are often modeled by sign(v) or smoothed sign approximations v/(Abs(v)+c), leading to stick-slip-like dynamics and non-sinusoidal waveforms.
- If dv_dt depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative (energy-like invariant possible); adding v-dependent terms generally breaks conservation and introduces decay or self-excitation.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO21)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: [5]
Matched candidates: ["c0*x + c1*v + c2*t + c3 + c4*v*sin(c5*x + c6) + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)"]

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v = 0.7675*sin(t) - 0.2639*v*sin(x)**

The GT has two terms:
1. A `sin(t)` term
2. A `v*sin(x)` term

Let me analyze each candidate to see if it can match this structure. For a match, the candidate must be able to produce exactly `sin(t)` and `v*sin(x)` terms, with all other terms zeroed out.

**Key observations:**
- `sin(t)` can come from `cos(t + c)` with `c = -π/2`, or `sin(t + c)` with `c = 0`
- `v*sin(x)` requires a product of `v` and `sin(x)`. Terms like `v*cos(c*t)` cannot produce `v*sin(x)`.
- Terms like `c*x`, `1/sqrt(x)`, `t`, constants can be zeroed by setting coefficients to 0.

Let me check each candidate systematically:

**Candidate 5:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*t + c3 + c4*v*sin(c5*x + c6) + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)`
- Set c0=0, c1=0, c2=0, c3=0
- `c4*v*sin(c5*x + c6)`: set c5=1, c6=0 → c4*v*sin(x). Set c4=-0.2639 ✓
- `c7*cos(c8*t + c9)`: set c8=1, c9=-π/2 → c7*sin(t). Set c7=0.7675 ✓
- **This matches!**

**Candidate 8:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*t + c3 + c4*sin(c5*x + c6) + c7*cos(c8*t + c9)`
- Has `sin(x)` but NOT multiplied by `v`. Cannot produce `v*sin(x)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 13:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*v + c3*x + c4*t + c5 + c6*cos(c7*t + c8)`
- Has `v` (linear) but no `v*sin(x)`. **No match.**

**Candidate 16:** `c0*x + c1*v + c2*cos(c3*t) + c4*t/(c5 + v) + c6*v*sin(c7*x + c8)`
- `c6*v*sin(c7*x + c8)`: set c7=1, c8=0 → v*sin(x) ✓
- `c2*cos(c3*t)`: set c3=1 → cos(t), but we need sin(t). cos(t) = sin(t+π/2)... wait, cos(c3*t) doesn't have a phase shift. But cos(t) ≠ sin(t). However, cos(-t) = cos(t), so no way to get sin(t) from cos(c3*t) alone without a phase.
- `c4*t/(c5 + v)`: this term can't be zeroed unless c4=0, but then we lose the sin(t) source.
- Set c0=0, c1=0, c4=0. Then we only have `c2*cos(c3*t) + c6*v*sin(x)`. cos(c3*t) ≠ sin(t). **No match.**

**Candidate 35:** `c0*x + c1*cos(c2*t) + c3/sqrt(x) + c4*t + c5 + c6*v*sin(c7*t + c8)`
- Has `v*sin(c7*t + c8)` — this is `v*sin(t)`, not `v*sin(x)`. **No match.**

Going through all remaining candidates similarly: most have `v*cos(c*t)` (not `v*sin(x)`), or lack the `v*sin(x)` term entirely. Only Candidate 5 has `v*sin(c5*x + c6)` combined with `cos(c8*t + c9)`.

After checking all 50 candidates carefully, only **Candidate 5** has both the required `v*sin(x)` and `sin(t)` basis functions.
